# Architecture Decision Records

Every architectural decision in outreach-factory has an ADR in this directory. Format: `NNNN-kebab-case-title.md`. Numbers are append-only; superseded ADRs are marked **Status: Superseded by ADR-NNNN**, never deleted.

Template: [`0000-template.md`](0000-template.md). Copy it to start a new ADR.

## When to write an ADR

Write one for any decision that:
- Changes the source-of-truth model for any piece of state (touches I1 in `docs/PILLAR-PLAN.md`).
- Introduces a new pillar primitive (policy rule class, migration runner phase, channel adapter, observability surface, etc.).
- Picks a load-bearing dependency or rejects a popular one (Alembic vs custom, OPA vs hand-rolled, OTel vs Prometheus-only, etc.).
- Changes a public API in `orchestrator/`.
- Resolves a risk register entry, or weakens an invariant in service of unblocking shipped work.

If you're refactoring within an established pattern, an ADR is overkill, so leave the rationale in the commit message.

## Pillar F was removed

The voice-corpus / embedding-retrieval and draft-quality subsystem (Pillar F, ADRs 0038 through 0049) is no longer part of the product. The de-AI step is now a fresh-context humanizer pass that rewrites the assembled draft against an anti-tell checklist plus a single reference example. There is no voice corpus, no embedding index, and no `sentence-transformers` dependency. The original Pillar F ADRs stay in the index below as immutable historical records (their status now reads Superseded); see the Pillar F removal ADR for the decision and rationale.

rejected: low-confidence-pattern tagging — premature optimization without observability data; rejected: probability-weighted sampling — non-deterministic, violates ADR-0026 D104 idempotence); confidence calibration per D125 — self-reported `confidence` field from the LLM response, clamped to [0.0, 1.0] (rejected: logprob via top_logprobs — not on Anthropic SDK as of 2026-05-23; rejected: benchmark-derived constants — Week 12 100-message benchmark is the right venue; rejected: ignore confidence — collapses important rule vs LLM distinction; rejected: bucketing — collapses information for downstream consumers); cost emit per D126 — `source: "reply_classifier_llm"` per ADR-0025 §I7's reservation, USD calculated from `COST_RATES_USD["anthropic"]`, `units = 1` per call matching Reoon/Gmail convention, emitted from `LLMFallbackClassifier.classify` BEFORE the `ClassifierResult` returns (Pass G then emits `reply_classified` after); per-prospect attribution via `person_id` from reply event; `run_id` deferred to Pillar I CLI; classifier-cap migration shape per D127 — `policy/0007_add_reply_classifier_llm_cap` writes ONE rule `reply-classifier-llm-monthly-cap` of type `budget.window-cap` with `source: reply_classifier_llm` + `window_days: 30` + `max_units: 50` (calibrated against Yang's expected ~30 long-tail uncategorized replies/month with 1.5-2.5× safety margin; at Haiku 4.5 rates ≈ $0.03/month — cap's role is operator visibility into LLM spend + runaway-call protection, not budget protection per se); follows Pillar C Weeks 7-10's commented-factory pattern; ONE rule per migration (structurally simpler than Week 11's bidirectional two-rule shape); SAME rule class as Weeks 7-10 (not Week 11's `cooldown.cross-channel-touch`); monthly window (distinct from Weeks 7-9's weekly + Week 10's daily); NO `block_when.channel:` (LLM is channel-agnostic — runs against reply events from every channel uniformly); commented factory matches LLM fallback's opt-in posture (Pass G accepts a `RuleBasedClassifier` by default; LLMFallbackClassifier constructed at wiring site; operators uncomment cap when they opt in); cross-pillar audit extension per D128 — new `classification_method: "llm"` shape in `reply_classified` events (Pass M's `category=unsubscribe` filter closed-by-construction because LLM never emits unsubscribe; Pass N + Pass C heal closed-by-design — they read category, not method; Pass G idempotence index closed-by-design — keyed on (reply_message_id, channel) not classification_method; Pillar G dashboards by-design broadening — EXPAND by intent) + new `cost_incurred.source=reply_classifier_llm` (BudgetWindowCapRule consumes via source filter; classifier-cap migration ships the operator-tunable rule; verdict: zero new P1/P2/P3 findings); R016 added to risk register (LLM cost runaway from inbox flood — mitigated by classifier-cap migration + operator-deliberate per-run cap defense-in-depth via existing BudgetPerRunCapRule class + opt-in posture at wiring layer); ≥3 rejected alternatives per decision + §Downstream pillar impact across E/F/G/H/I/J + §Migration/rollout + §Existing-operator seed (Shape A canonical / Shape B renamed / Shape new-operator — simpler than Week 11's four-shape catalog); ONE new policy migration `policy/0007_add_reply_classifier_llm_cap` (reversible; round-trip byte-identical against real factory template; pending count moves 16 → 17); 60 new reply_classifier_llm unit tests in `tests/test_reply_classifier_llm.py` (LLMResponse construction invariants + build_llm_prompt template with the load-bearing unsubscribe-exclusion language verbatim + compute_llm_cost_usd against pricing table + build_cost_incurred_payload shape per ADR-0006 + _parse_llm_response_text accepting clean JSON + markdown fences + integer confidence + clamping out-of-range confidence — CRITICAL: refuses-loud at parse layer if LLM returns `unsubscribe` per D123 second defense-in-depth layer; | [0034](0034-pillar-e-email-verification-cache.md) | Pillar E Week 4-5 — email-verification cache primitive (the second cost-avoidance pillar primitive per ADR-0032 D144; ships `orchestrator/email_verification_cache.py`); module placement per D154 — top-level sibling of `enrich_emails.py` + `discovery_dedup.py` mirroring ADR-0033 D149's `discovery_dedup.py` precedent (rejected: inside `enrich_emails.py` — conflates cache-as-prevention with verification-as-action + inflates module surface; `email_verification_cache_hit` event class emit-shape per D155 — carries `person_id` (cached event's person_id, defaulting via factory; caller-override available) + `email` (the looked-up address) + `cached_result` (Reoon status STRING — `"safe"` / `"catch_all"` / `"invalid"` / `"disposable"` / etc.; co-emission would double-count in Pillar G dashboards (rejected: stamp `channel: "none"` mirroring dedup — operator-confusing, excludes cache hits from per-email-channel dashboards; rejected: omit channel field — violates channel-on-every-event invariant; when caller opts in via `led`, function performs cache prelude + becomes sole authoritative emitter of cost_incurred + cache_hit events); a cache-lookup failure (corrupt ledger; index error) MUST NOT block verification — wrapper falls through to Reoon HTTP with stderr warning (cache-as-FAST-PATH discipline per HANDOFF-pillar-e-week-4.md §Design-decisions); the backfill event class is NEW (`type: "enrolled_source_skill_backfill"` + `person_id` + `source_skill` (normalized from legacy `enrolled.source` via `normalize_legacy_source_to_skill`) + `_backfill_of_ts` (the original event's `ts` for pairing) + `_recovered_by: "migration_0007_..."` + `channel: "none"` + `_emitted_by: "discovery_lineage"`); 3. else look for paired backfill event; 4. else inline-normalize via `normalize_legacy_source_to_skill`); the rename `enrolled.source` → `enrolled.source_skill` is implemented additively at the emit side — `enroll_person` emits BOTH `source` (back-compat) AND `source_skill` (canonical) on every new enrolled event (the values carry the same normalized value); mismatch is caller bug) → per-dimension refuse-loud raises `Layer4GuardRefusal` (subclass of ValueError) when state='refused' AND override absent → construct payload (rejected: separate per-dimension factories with top-level combinator — splits SYMMETRIC verdict + risks two events per draft; rejected: Optional[dict] return — silent-None hides caller bugs; rejected: tuple override kwarg — operator-hostile positional + loses per-dimension naming; rejected: cfg dict carrying overrides — type-checker blind on required-when-override-true). `Layer4GuardRefusal` typed exception per D245 — subclass of ValueError (existing try/except blocks continue working) + carries `refused_dimensions` tuple + per-Layer 2 result objects for operator-readable diagnostic surfacing. `draft_ready` event class per D246 — FOURTH Pillar F event class per ADR-0038 D182 joining `voice_exemplar_retrieved` (Week 2) + `hallucination_detected` (Week 6) + `draft_quality_scored` (Week 8); emit-only-on-both-pass posture (DISTINCT from Week 6's emit-only-on-uncited per ADR-0043 D219 + Week 8's emit-always per ADR-0045 D231) — the event SIGNALS dispatch-eligibility, the refuse-case is the loud `Layer4GuardRefusal`; D279 `observability_class_uncatalogued` diagnostic emit semantics — single event class with `kind` field; values closed-set `_DIAGNOSTIC_KINDS = frozenset({"uncatalogued", "missing_ts"})`; at-most-ONE per kind per call (max two emits per call); the ts-missing posture is REFUSE-LOUD per the audit's recommendation; payload carries first-seen `offending_type` + total `count` + `channel: null` + `_emitted_by: "observability"` audit marker per ADR-0010 D17 (mirrors `_recovered_by` audit marker on Pass C per ADR-0049 D262); the kind="missing_ts" variant additionally carries first-seen `person_id` (if any) (rejected: separate event class `observability_event_missing_ts` — extends `OBSERVABILITY_NEW_EVENT_CLASSES` closed-set commitment; would amend the Week 1 foundation's two-member closed-set; the audit recommended single-class extension; rejected: silent-skip — violates I7 refuse-loud convention; rejected: refuse-loud at the call boundary via `ValueError`-on-ts-missing — breaks dashboard rendering instead of surfacing producer bug; rejected: per-call hard cap of 10 emits across both kinds — wastes the per-kind distinction). D280 deterministic snapshot ordering — snapshots sorted alphabetically by `event_class` (deterministic across consecutive calls against fixed ledger state per ADR-0031 D140 + ADR-0050 D276(a)); `per_breakdown_counts` constructed via `dict(sorted(...))` so Python 3.7+'s insertion-order = iteration-order guarantees operators read ascending alphabetical keys (rejected: random/insertion-order — violates determinism contract; rejected: per-pillar grouping — couples to per-pillar foundation ADR's event-class enumeration order; rejected: sort by `total_count` descending — run-time-dependent ordering violates byte-identical contract). D281 channel-on-every-event invariant — `MetricSnapshot.channel` = single non-null channel value if every in-window event of the class carries that channel value; None otherwise (no channel field on events, OR multiple distinct channel values, OR a mix of channel + no-channel events); operators wanting per-channel breakdown pass `breakdown_by=("channel",)`; the `_BREAKDOWN_DIMS_ALLOWED` channel inclusion (already in the Week 1 ship) gets a regression-barrier test (rejected: one snapshot per (event_class, channel) pair — N×M-ifies snapshot list; per-Person dashboards see ~50 × ~4 = ~200 snapshots per call vs ~50; rejected: always set `MetricSnapshot.channel = None` — operator-ergonomic homogeneous case lost; rejected: refuse-loud on pathological "mix of channel-present and channel-missing" case at Week 2 — deferred to Week 3+ when per-event-class channel-required catalog could be made explicit).
